commit 4d675bdc19cc7520e8005303512f6b16d5d29529
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 4 03:04:13 2021 +0200

    City defense bonuses only in territory of war allies
    
    When a unit is attacked in a city or fort owned by a third party, the unit is a city defender only if the third party is also at war with the attacker, i.e. city defense and attack modifiers don't apply if the city owner is neutral (rationale: because the neutral city is not being attacked). [advc.183]
    
    BtS had allowed city defense in neutral territory except for forts. In AdvCiv I had, by accident, already disabled some of the defensive modifiers in cities (regardless of the at-war status of the third party); so this AdvCiv bug should be fixed now.

commit b25510b1a22f768af80ad422e617bd9a071f1503
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 4 02:50:26 2021 +0200

    Halve AI deal cancellation memory when AI cancels
    
    That is, when Open Borders or Defensive Pact is canceled by one side, the other side (if it's an AI civ) refuses to renew the deal for, on average, 10 turns (no change) and the side that canceled the deal (if it's an AI civ) refuses a new deal for 5 turns on average. [advc.130j]
    
    Should make it a bit less frustrating when the AI cancels OB due to AI diplo attitude dipping below the OB threshold.

commit e38523c668ec6b684c70c537efaefe9e25aa3fee
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 4 02:38:11 2021 +0200

    Earlier extra AI city defender on highest difficulty levels
    
    Around the start of the Medieval era instead of Renaissance. Sort of in response to item 2 in this CFC post:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/beating-advciv-diety-screenshots-discussion.668187/#post-16051984
    I don't think this change goes far enough to help the AI in the situation described (Classical era?). Generally, considering that the AI unit production discounts are smaller in AdvCiv, I think the AI is better off not wasting early-game production on defenders for minor non-border cities, even if that means that human players can sometimes sneak up on those cities (which sounds like a fun stratagem too). [advc.107]

commit f48687a63ffb48e5e6fed45b27341e6b039b51c5
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jun 30 17:46:24 2021 +0200

    Separate AgentIterator types for AI and non-AI civs
    
    So that AI headers don't need to be included in non-AI code that uses the iterators. This hadn't been a problem so far because many of the non-AI implementation files need to include the AI headers in any case, - but this isn't and shouldn't be a given. Also, I had originally assumed that the agent instance obtained from an iterator would usually be assigned to some kLoopPlayer variable in the body of the loop, so that a distinction between AI and non-AI code would be made at that point (i.e. by giving kLoopPlayer type CvPlayerAI& only in AI code and CvPlayer& otherwise), but I've come to prefer using the iterator directly.

commit 63d1e21db1d6f0c13cf1db6584518887bf45fae9
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jun 30 17:28:13 2021 +0200

    SparseEnumMap class, mainly for per-civ data at CvPlot
    
    Scarcely makes a difference with an 18-civ limit, but seems to speed up AI turns by some 15% with a 31-civ limit. The penalty for allowing 31 civs while playing only with 18 is now down to less than 10% on Earth18 (super-Huge map) in a test, and should hopefully be less than 5% on regular Huge maps (was 8% in a test prior to this change). [advc.enum]

    Fix potential OOS issue with sea patrol option
    
    The BUG option (introduced by AdvCiv) affects both human and AI players. In a network game, if only one player enables sea patrol, I expect that the game will go OOS when the AI starts a sea patrol mission (or once the sea patrol mission is triggered by a pillager).
    
    Now sea patrol is always disabled in network games, regardless of the BUG option. [advc.004k]

commit 4130e508264f1341c9788efb700148be344e3372
Author: f1rpo <27625493+f1rpo@users.noreply.github.com>
Date:   Wed May 5 23:55:41 2021 +0000

    PerfectMongoose (PM) update (#2)
    
    I've essentially rebased my earlier AdvCiv changes from PM 3.2 onto PM 3.3 (extracted from MongooseMod 4.2a) and, in the process, revised many of the AdvCiv changes. I've ended up replacing or reverting the bulk of the PM 3.3 additions. Perhaps the main novelty that I've kept is that PM 3.3 takes distances between continents into account when splitting the map into a New World and Old World for the "Old World Starts" option. PM 3.3 also makes several tweaks and bugfixes in the (start) tile evaluation functions -- but I'm mostly letting the DLL handle the starting positions, so these aren't significant improvements. However, reviewing the PM 3.3 changes was instructive for tackling some issues that I had been meaning to address for some time.
    
    For river placement, I'm now combining the standard river generator (DLL) with the PM river generator. And I've tweaked the PM generator to discourage rivers in extreme latitudes. This seems to achieve a reasonable spread of rivers and overall frequency. (The PM generator, on its own, tends to concentrate rivers in the tropics while leaving swaths of temperate land mostly dry.)
    
    When splitting up the map for the Old World Starts option, shallow-water connections and (as a coarse predictor of habitibility) latitude are now taken into account. Inspired by Toffer's C2C_World.py, the sea level now gets recalculated while trying to break a New World continent off of a Pangaea. Through these and some smaller changes, the Old World Starts option now seems to succeed somewhat reliably (at least more often than not?) at reserving a sizable New World, and no longer leads to an unpredictable land-sea ratio. AdvCiv's starting position algorithm [advc.027] now handles the assignment of starting sites even when playing with Old World Starts: PM reserves New World continents, and the DLL does all the rest based on that constraint.
    
    Fixed some problems at the map boundaries, in particular hills and peaks caused by "attenuation" near the poles. And tweaked the slope-based method for placing peaks and hills so as to discourage large clumps, coastal elevations and straight, uninterrupted mountain chains.
    
    Snow hills can again - rarely - occur in temperate latitudes to represent alpine areas. Apart from that, Tundra and Snow are confined to their appropriate latitudes, with more varied boundary regions than in AdvCiv 0.99. (Although the boundaries are sometimes still straighter than I'd like.) In part, this has been accomplished through a change adopted from C2C_World.py that adjusts per-tile temperature values to the tile's distance from the sea. There is now also a timberline running through the Tundra.
    
    The PerfectWorld 2 landmass generator is available as an option (as it was in the original script; AdvCiv had removed that option along with several others). Seems to work well enough but, unfortunately, isn't much better at generating massive continents than the (default) Perlin noise generator. Both generators can produce large continents, but usually in a snaky shape that impedes interactions (warfare) between the civs. This remains an open issue; I don't think tweaks to the existing parameters can resolve this.
    
    I've held off on the removal of map options and on changes specific to the AdvCiv DLL until the last few commits in the pull request. This should make it easy to obtain a version of the script that is portable to other mods.

commit f8fc332f4c60032947f1336b9b28bb1095951456

commit 4ae382e5dbec429eddcc84e08935e3f94d01a20a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Mar 20 23:37:23 2021 +0100

    Revised all code in the UWAI component
    
    ... and also AdvCiv4lerts.
    
    I've tested this a bit; looks like there can't be many new bugs left. Will have to do a side-by-side review of the changes later (and do a lot more testing); for now I just want to have it committed.
    
    The style now conforms with the style that I use in the rest of the GameCore DLL. Floating-point numbers been replaced almost entirely with fixed-point numbers (ScaledNum), in the UWAI component and in all other synchronized code, the exception being a couple of uses of std::log and the (BtS/ Lead From Behind) combat odds calculations. if nothing else, this seems to have improved performance - though other factors could be responsible for that as well. A lot of low-level refactoring, some bugfixes; the important ones, I'll commit separately on another branch.

commit ccefc3a0497ab847cb6bbe5ae7b4692d47301646
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Feb 16 20:58:29 2021 +0100

    Fix problems with improvement upgrade rate
    
    Fixed a K-Mod bug that had caused the AI to value cottages /less/ highly when in Emancipation. (At least I'm pretty sure that this was wrong. Let's hope.) [advc.001]
    
    Count the improvement upgrade rate at times-100 precision so that the Emancipation ability works as expected for values that aren't a multiple of 100 and for negative values (so long as they're not less than -100, i.e. still can't let Hamlets decay back to Cottages). [advc.912f]
    
    To make this work, the number of turns that an improvement has been worked is now also counted at times-100 precision. This requires an int counter instead of a short int, but I've kept the size of CvPlot (kind of important for cache performance) the same as before by replacing another int with a char.

commit e8bfef1ca5cd2c188c2ad01365760ed750a7b3bc
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Tue Feb 16 19:57:54 2021 +0100

    Refactor combat odds calc, damage limit bugfix
    
    Move the getCombatOdds and LFBgetCombatOdds functions into a new translation unit, split them up so that they can share some code with each other and so that the Advanced Combat Odds mod (ACO) can also reuse some of it. (To be done in another commit: Throw out the code now in calculateCombatOddsLegacy, move the ACO code.) Refactored all the odds-related code, but mostly just the variable names (which had made the ACO code quite difficult to comprehend).
    
    Primarily, this should make it more feasible for mod-mods to change the combat rules. (Updating the odds calculations is a real obstacle to that.)
    
    Added code for verifying the calculated odds through simulations of the combat resolution procedure. Found one bug this way, which had already been fixed in ACO (i.e. the displayed odds were wrong only when ACO was disabled): The BtS/ Lead From Behind odds had assumed that combat ends when the attacker's damage limit is reached, but combat resolution actually requires the limit to be exceeded. This matters for example when a Cannon attacks another Cannon because the damage limit (80) is then a multiple of the per-round damage.
    
    I've chosen to fix the bug by changing the combat resolution procedure -- combat now ends upon reaching the combat limit. I've updated the ACO code accordingly. The hit that reaches the damage limit is now also included in the Combat Log. [advc.001l]

commit 8b3371a65e89457a745d66e7bc1e226e1759ebbe
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jan 31 04:39:59 2021 +0100

    Stricter conditions for AI opening borders for naval trade
    
    A revealed land tile now only makes an AI civ willing to open its borders if the tile is on the same landmass as a city owned by the AI civ. If it's on a different landmass, then there needs to be a trade connection (via Sailing or Astronomy). The AI will also open its borders if it has a unit adjacent to a tile that it can't currently enter but will be able to enter through an OB agreement. (And, as before, the AI is willing to open its borders regardless of accessibility if its attitude level is one above the threshold set in XML.) [advc.124]

commit f849392ff4bf6c12df0d8e609ca0946e5206618d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jan 13 21:26:33 2021 +0100

    UWAI: Fix some issues with AI capitulation decisions
    
    These changes should align the "not right now" response (computed quickly on the human turn by CvTeamAI) better with the decisions made by the UWAI component (on the AI turn).
    
    And, in situations when an AI civ is fighting multiple wars, the all-war-ending effect of a capitulation is now taken into account. (Not reliably, but I hope it'll work well enough most of the time.)
    
    Also fixes a flipped sign (wasn't terribly consequential though).
    
    To address problems apparent from the savegames posted here:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/quick-advciv-questions-answers.666137/#post-15997844

commit 074c73cd051b8e3c683b02447b1d983a66856b9f

Date:   Wed Jan 13 21:20:49 2021 +0100

    UWAI: Tweak "public opposition" aspect of war utility
    
    I think this had too much impact when war weariness got really bad. Also reduced the impact when close to a military victory. This was one of several problems in the savegames posted here:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/quick-advciv-questions-answers.666137/#post-15997844

commit 68196b1cd152615955a0cbece59f8987acdfc5d6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed Jan 13 21:14:37 2021 +0100

    UWAI: Tweak "loathing" aspect of war utility calculation
    
    Disregard the loathing aspect when expecting to be eliminated soon. This should prevent the AI from continuing suicidal wars just to inconvenience an enemy.
    
    When computing war utility from the point of view of a human civ (relevant e.g. for peace terms), don't completely disregard the loathing aspect, i.e. assume that human players are to an extent vengeful.

commit 529ebb7b4f59681b609c10c4d3ad31838ba62d67
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Dec 17 23:35:17 2020 +0100

    Improve AI support for mods with custom eras
    
    Some new tags in Civ4EraInfos.xml through which mods can tell the AI e.g. in which era (if any) oceangoing ships become available. And a tag that allows mods to map any custom eras to the BtS era numbers (0 to 6) so that the AI is aware that e.g. era #1 is in the midgame when a mod has only 3 eras. [advc.erai]
    
    Inspired by this Kek-Mod commit:
    DarkLunaPhantom/Civ4-K-Mod@8b9aecdd4cfabb393d0bba3f3ed77cb2cd78a680
    (I've directly adopted one small AI change concerning the counting of religions, under change id [kekm.36].)
    
    Also added a tag that enables all techs of an era as goody hut outcomes, thus making part of change [advc.314] configurable through XML.
    
    And a bunch of minor refactoring changes. (I've gone through all instances of the word "Era" in the AI code, so a lot of style irregularities have caught my eye.)

commit 9a623ad895c73c2ce0fe4d5f5cf668ab04848307
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sat Dec 12 15:43:15 2020 +0100

    Let SPI handle team games, plus other changes to starting sites
    
    Greedy algorithm for assigning starting sites in team games added to the StartingPositionIteration (SPI) class. The BtS algorithm is still used for improving on the greedy solution. Also refactored the BtS algorithm (superficially). SPI still isn't used for team games with a high player count and high average team size - because the greedy algorithm doesn't handle that well (and the BtS algorithm does OK). [advc.027]
    
    The BtS algorithm for swapping around starting sites in team games is now executed right after the initial assignment of starting sites, i.e. it's no longer part of the normalization step. [advc.108b]
    
    Starting site handicaps from the difficulty setting (StartingLocPercent) now also apply to team games. This is implemented by applying the average handicap of each team to all its members. [advc.108b]
    
    SPI now respects tiles marked as "StartingPlot" in scenarios that allow arbitrary civ leaders (e.g. Africa). SPI only finds additional starting sites when there are too few pre-marked sites. (That can easily happen; e.g. the base-game version of Europe has only 6 pre-marked starting sites.) [advc.027]
    
    SPI now handles starting sites for players with the "RandomStartLocation" attribute set in a scenario file; except for scenarios with fixed civ leaders (CvInitCore::getWBMapNoPlayers()==false), which SPI still doesn't interfere with. [advc.027]
    
    Dialed down the randomization of found-city values when picking a "RandomStartLocation". [advc.027]

commit 96c6996a71eeef103f2a7895347afad913a09d53

    [change id advc.158]
    
    Moved into a separate class. Enabled for humans (and minor civs) because I think the only potential OOS issues with humans are in Debug-mode help text (fixed by this commit; change advc.001n) and in the cost function of the pathfinder (already addressed by karadoc). commit 95e434343b1242b86138b89ac3a64de29d194160
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Nov 12 02:02:36 2020 +0100

    Revise AI_targetCityVal
    
    ... i.e. how the AI decides which enemy city to target. Now based on UWAI data (specifically: path distances, AI_assetVal). I've kept most of the old code as a fallback because the UWAI cache isn't always up to date (and for the K-Mod/Legacy AI option). [advc.104d]
    
    Unless the attacker is very powerful militarily, AI_targetCityVal now prefers cities with low tile defense and (for naval assaults) continents with few enemy cities.
    
    Added some ad-hoc code for targeting the enemy's strategic resources. (A proper evaluation of a resource from the enemy's point of view - and whether conquering the city will flip the resource tile - would be too much work.)
    
    Per-area target cities are now updated when AI war plans change.
    
    Reduced the value assigned to Shrines in AI_assetVal. This is relevant for UWAI, AI_targetCityVal and AI_citTradeVal. The K-Mod evaluation is sensible, but I don't think it was on the right scale.
    
    The Barbarians no longer pick a permanent (per-continent) target city. [advc.300]
    
    The AI can no longer pick target cities that are neither revealed nor deducible. This visibility cheat was probably inadvertent. [advc.001]
    
    TeamPathFinder can now reuse allocated memory even if the team (for which paths are generated) changes. I'm not making use of this after all though because resetting the node data in between pathfinder calls is still a bit too slow, and pathfinding in AI_targetCityVal isn't really needed; the distance information from the UWAI cache suffices. [advc.pf]

That's a BtS bug. The blue circles had also prevented AdvCiv from showing resource-layer bubbles for goody huts. [advc.004z]

commit fc7640933b544f0f943f527e2edc08999da1dc00
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Oct 25 23:36:14 2020 +0100

    Let sea and air units enter rival forts through OB
    
    In order to make forts more similar to cities, streamlining the rules. Also addressed a minor oddity with unowned forts: They had been granting +25% tile defense but didn't enable city defense modifiers (e.g. Garrison promotion). Now all defensive advantages apply to unowned forts. [advc.183]
    
    In the process, I've replaced the CvPlot member functions isCity(bool,TeamTypes), isFriendlyCity, isEnemyCity, isValidDomainForLocation, isValidDomainForAction with CvTeam and CvUnit member functions. The new functions fix some minor (BtS) information leaks by distinguishing between revealed and unrevealed improvement type. Change ids advc.124, advc.299 are affected by these refactoring changes.
    
    The Fortify action is no longer recommended for foreign cities. (Those recommendations were unwise and had leaked information.) [advc.004]
    
    Also slightly refactored and tweaked the AI checks for ships (in a city or fort) being threatened from land. [advc.139]

commit 6102c9181ff39e45daffa060675b89dc21c5d69c
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

    Prefer starting sites with a resource just out of reach
    
    Only when StartingPositionIteration (SPI) is enabled. Increase the found-city value a bit when there is a resource or other high-yield tile just outside the city radius. (This doesn't by any means guarantee that every player will find such a resource near their starting site.) In order to make the decision whether to move the starting settler more interesting. It's the first decision in the game and SPI had made settling in place optimal most of the time. [advc.027]

commit f429f6e13054084feaa84c996cc891e55abc6243
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 19 04:02:33 2020 +0200

    Fix AdvCiv bug: unique range of resources ignored
    
    Introduced in AdvCiv 0.97. There are two iUnique tags that are supposed to enforce a minimum distance in between resources. One for resource classes (e.g. Livestock), one for resources (e.g. Cow). The latter had been ignored. The most easily observable effect was that Fish resources (they're especially common) had appeared next to each other; they're supposed to be 2 tiles apart. For strategic resources, there was still the unique range from the bonus class to fall back on.
    
    Bug report (I guess):
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/goto/post?id=15829227#post-15829227

commit 68ebb86656a7f84772b499520e517039341940ce
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 19 03:35:24 2020 +0200

    Randomize tile for normalizeAddFood; prefer inner ring.
    
    [change id advc.108]
    
    The tile for food resources placed during normalization was, shockingly, not randomized. The choice of the food resource wasn't randomized either, but that has already been changed in AdvCiv 0.97. When possible, BtS had just placed Corn east of the starting site.
    
    normalizeAddExtras had already been choosing random tiles. Both functions now have a bias for the inner ring. Because this gives players more leeway to move the starting settler.

commit 48e93752d05a44c167cc994101bc2e6cc8a2caa0
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jul 19 02:58:53 2020 +0200

    Don't place unreachable water resources
    
    Water tiles that could only be worked from a city on an impassable tile (Peak) are counted as unworkable, meaning that they have 0 yield and no resources can be placed there. [advc.129d]
    
    Not covered: Water tiles workable by a city - but fully enclosed by Ice and thus not reachable for Work Boats. Such tiles shouldn't receive resources, but that's not so easy to prevent.

commit 86cc0d11ab0fd8ede90cd81957f7a69a988661e5

commit e4e936ce468c2f548325e50ac01f2d45f3463c76
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu Jul 16 22:31:59 2020 +0200

    Show map rand, sync rand seed in Debug mode
    
    [change id advc.027b]
    
    That is, store the initial seed, and show it in Debug mode if Ctrl is held down when hovering over the big flag on the main screen. So that map generation can be reproduced even when no initial seeds were set in CivilizationIV.ini -- by reading the randomly generated seeds off the flag button and entering them in CivilizationIV.ini. This could become helpful for dealing with user feedback on the starting position iteration algorithm.
    
    Changed the normalization code so that only map rand is used; in BtS, it's a mix of map rand and sync rand, and that gets in the way of reproducing regenerated maps.
    
    And a small tweak to [advc.108]: Jungle on a resource in the ring of tiles surrounding a starting city radius is now cleared with a probability of 1/2 instead of 2/3.

commit cb93c6bbae49b5b8ce6c4432d21d6e25a72fbba6
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jun 28 21:59:12 2020 +0200

    Tweak lake placement near starting sites
    
    [change id advc.108]
    
    When adding a lake for freshwater during the normalization step, tiles adjacent to the starting site are now (strictly) preferred. BtS had also done that, but K-Mod had randomized the placement of lakes (without regard for the distance from the starting site; probably an oversight by karadoc).
    
    Since the AI knows how to move its starting settler, no freshwater source gets added during normalization if there is already a freshwater tile adjacent to the starting site (i.e. a freshwater source two tiles away from the starting site).
    This change can be disabled through NORMALIZE_STARTPLOTS_AGGRESSIVELY=1 in GlobalDefines_advc.xml.
    Note: Even if a player chooses not to move the settler onto a freshwater tile, adjacent freshwater can still be useful for irrigation.
    
    When the game decides whether a starting site needs extra food, Whale is no longer counted as an available food source (unless starting in Renaissance or later). [advc.001]

commit 82c08218c66b1a01049f4bf81647a77ab3949573
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jun 28 21:01:25 2020 +0200

    More tweaks, fixed miscalculations for starting positions
    
    I've now seen decent results for a variety of single-player maps. The new algorithm (starting position iteration, SPI) is now enabled by default -- although more testing is needed.
    
    Made not_too_Big_or_Small maps smaller again because SPI is now more willing to let civs start on the small landmasses. [advc.165]
    
    Slightly increased the land-to-sea ratio of PerfectMongoose because, even without the Old World Starts option, there is typically a fair amount of land that civs can't access at game start and the landmasses where civs do start were a bit too crowded; SPI didn't handle it well. Also decreased the recommended player count (shown on the Custom Game screen) for the Old World Starts option because PerfectMongoose usually fails to reserve a large continent for the New World. (That's a problem for another day; changing the recommendation is only a band-aid.) [advc.021b]
    
    When re-assigning starting sites based on handicap, the game now tries to avoid giving human players a site for which SPI has computed a high "volatility" value. Being very close to another site, being isolated and reliance on early colonization contribute to the volatility of a site. (The re-assignment algorithm doesn't go out of its way far here, so volatile human starts are still very much a possibility.)

commit cbc97b79b3c2833d2ccf82c9e485374ef82715a9

Date:   Mon Jun 22 00:54:28 2020 +0200

    Tweak AI power values of military buildings
    
    Production buildings like Forge no longer contribute to military power because they're already covered by the production graph, which, in K-Mod/AdvCiv, also factors into AI war planning. [advc.131c]

    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/thoughts-on-pyramids-and-other-wonder-discussion.659502/#post-15806318

commit d6ea7fc8701bfe2d4353437da01e5d5b392d8b7e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jun 21 23:14:06 2020 +0200

    Starting positions (cont.), normalization.
    
    Completed the starting position iteration (SPI) algorithm (yet to be documented in the manual), but still need to test it on various maps and probably make adjustments based on those tests. For now SPI is disabled by default through GlobalDefines_advc.xml. Log output is disabled through the DLL (StartingPositionsIteration.cpp). [advc.027]
    
    Modified PerfectMongoose so that SPI can work on it. [advc.027]
    
    Made Not Too Big Or Small a little larger again (partly reverting [advc.165]) because it seems that SPI will usually place most civs on the "Big" landmass. (I'm still trying to figure out if that's really the most balanced way to set that map up.)
    
    Starting site "normalization" is now done based on byproducts of SPI (if it is enabled). Specifically, the SPI data fully determines the placement of extra resources and features (forest, oasis, flood plains) and has some (small) impact on the placement of additional food near sites where food isn't already abundant. The reassignment of starting sites based on difficulty (StartingLocPercent) also uses SPI data. [advc.027]
    
    Made some other functional and refactoring changes to normalization: [advc.108]
    - Far fewer extra forests are placed. BtS basically places forests everywhere when a site's found value is too low. That looks conspicuous and doesn't help much. Greater care is also taken not to place too many flood plains.
    - When placing extra resources, resource types that already exist in the city radius are probabilistically avoided, especially in tiles adjacent to the existing resource, and especially for resources that don't normally form groups.
    - Avoid placing food as extra resources when a site already has enough food and just needs to be buffed.
    - Coastal seafood resources now count as "high-food" resources when deciding whether a starting site has enough food.
    - Normalization may add at most 2 hills (up to a total of 3 as in BtS).
    - Additional (non-water) food and hills have to be placed on the same landmass as the capital (from PerfectMongoose/ PerfectWorld2); other extra resources also aren't placed on other landmasses - if it can be avoided.
    - Gold can no longer be placed as an extra resource.
    
    The normalization step tries to avoid placing resources on goody huts; removes the hut if it can't be avoided. (Stacking resources with huts isn't good because the resource layer also shows hut icons in AdvCiv.) [advc.004z]

commit 0b14bcd679b516c5734fc4b184830eb7ad28f79a
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Jun 22 00:48:55 2020 +0200

    PerfectMongoose: Disable minimum-hill logic.
    
    The DLL code for extra hills is adequate. And a few non-functional changes. [advc.021b]

commit a527ee47f63b521109e0a891f0fcb9d837476a8b
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Jun 21 22:18:00 2020 +0200

    Fix AdvCiv bug with MP turn timer getting enabled in SP
    
    I still don't know what had caused this problem and at what point I've introduced it; hopefully only recently. Apparently the multiplayer option array was sometimes, randomly, not initialized or became deallocated. I've made sure that this can't occur anymore by replacing the array with an EnumMap. Actually, I've replaced almost all CvInitCore arrays with EnumMaps and, while I was at it, made refactoring changes all over the class.

commit 2d7f8162159a2f7c7ca8c556835c1bea0bfa139d

commit 96d6710603295e681a1ee208c101a5d978df1d74
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri May 29 17:39:50 2020 +0200

    Improve how AI deals with units that can't enter all terrain
    
    Fix a BtS bug in the evaluation of Astronomy; no utility had been counted for the ability of Galleons to enter ocean. [advc.001]
    
    The rest [advc.057] should only be relevant for mod-mods. Addresses problems reported here:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-35#post-15775795
    
    - Instead of just counting the impassable terrain and feature types, a fingerprint is computed (so that the AI can tell that e.g. a unit unable to enter Desert isn't necessarily compatible with one unable to enter Snow). An 3-bit impassable count is prepended to the fingerprint - to allow ordering units by their impassable counts.
    
    - The AI ensures that no unit in a group has a higher impassable count than the unit leading the group. Meaning that leading units are always the least flexible unit in a group wrt. movement restrictions. This is accomplished by disallowing units that would violate the invariant stated above from joining.
    
    - When a human civ comes under AI control (e.g. AI Auto Play), groups that don't satisfy the invariant are split up. AI code for handling human-AI status changes is now also called by the Change Player component (Alt+Z) [advc.127c] and the Rise & Fall component [advc.700]. Meaning that groups are split up if necessary and the AI attitude cache is updated. This was previously not being done after Alt+Z and had lead to failed assertions.

Date:   Fri May 29 17:00:48 2020 +0200

commit a70e4ce3a1db01c51da7fa370a706d8784191b38
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Thu May 28 00:44:41 2020 +0200

    Algorithm for fairer starting positions (wip)
    
    Looks like I've committed a few changes to CvGame already in some earlier commit. Oh well. The whole shebang is for now disabled through CvGame::assignStartingPlots. (And even if it were enabled, the only effect would be a second or two of pointless computations.)
    
    Implemented in StartingPositionIteration.cpp. It's still somewhat unclear how the iteration part will work.
    
    Integration: The BtS starting position will be used as the initial solution of the iterative algorithm. Map scripts that override assignStartingPlots or findStartingPlot take precedence, i.e. the new code gets disabled then. I've made an exception for Pangaea, which really doesn't need custom code for its starting positions. If a script overrides findStartingArea, then my algorithm will restrict itself to sites on landmasses where BtS has placed starting sites.
    
    The preliminaries (computed only once upfront) are done:
    
    a) Some ten potential starting sites per civ that the main algorithm will choose from - computed through a mix of maximizing found-city values and "clearing the neighborhood".
    
    b) Function evaluateWorkablePlot added to CitySiteEvaluator for evaluating individual plots as opposed to all plots around a city site. The new function uses mostly subroutines of my AIFoundValue class. I've refactored the code a bit to avoid duplication. Also some tweaks:
    - Financial trait is now disregarded (like all other traits) when evaluating starting sites. [advc.031]
    - Fix a bug in [advc.031] - multiple resources of the same (previously unavailable) type in the city radius had not been recognized as surplus resources.
    - Use a flatter distribution of per-tile weights when placing a capital - because capitals tend to grow large.
    - Starting sites with a high number of bad tiles are more strongly discouraged. [advc.108]
    
    c) Table with path distances between all potential sites and all non-negligible workable plots (~1000 on a Standard-size map). Computed through Dijkstra's algorithm with a distance metric that allows steps from land to coastal water and from coastal water to ocean, but makes those moves (very) expensive.
    
    Tbd.: a), b) and c) will be combined into a "start value" for each civ and, from the distribution of those start values, a fairness value will be computed. That's what the main algorithm is supposed to optimize, and the fairness value should also affect the "normalization" step in the end.

commit 2a15829d174d621f75f3de2ea904e303fe0cb782
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Wed May 27 22:16:40 2020 +0200

    Add enum type for plot ids
    
    [advc.enum]
    
    To be done: An iterator for traversing all map plots. One can do this now:
    FOR_EACH_ENUM(PlotNum)
    {
       CvPlot const& p = GC.getMap().plotNum(eLoopPlotNum);
       // ...
    }
    But that's still pretty awkward. I've mainly added PlotNumTypes for EnumMap. Internally, EnumMap will use short int for PlotNumTypes. This means, future code will break when a map has more than 32768 tiles. I'm not aware of a playable scenario with that many tiles, but the "Giant" Earth scenarios come kind of close. If MAX_CIV_PLAYERS has been increased beyond 18, EnumMap uses __int32 for PlotNumTypes. Let's hope that no one will try to play a 200x200 map with just 18 civs.

    Separate flag for normalization in CitySiteEvaluator

commit f086293436683a67c24ca769372d8bbbb8593503
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Fri Apr 24 21:59:44 2020 +0200

    Clean up "concealed player identity" mess
    
    [change id advc.058]
    
    K-Mod had changed CvPlayer::getName, getPlayerColor and the two getCivDescription functions so that they return "unknown" or the Barbarian color for players whom the active (human) player hasn't met or seen yet. That has been leading to some problems now and then, and it turns out that it's not a workable approach at all for the Rise & Fall component, which collects interface messages sent to AI civs in case that the human player will later take control of those civs. The player names and colors in those messages mustn't be based on the active player. Bug report:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-32#post-15739533
    
    Now the true names and colors are returned again by default, and there are separate functions getKnownName, getKnownPlayerColor etc. for the few situations in which identities may have to be concealed. Hopefully, I've correctly identified those situations.
    
    And refactored CvPlayerColorInfo so that it uses ColorTypes instead of int.

    [change id advc.101]
    
    Indicate hurry anger, draft anger, foreign religion (if not being countered by owner's state religion) in the hover text of the nationality bar. The text doesn't say by how much these factors increase foreign culture strength; too complicated to implement.
    
    Decrease the impact of hurry and draft anger. Previously, a city was treated as having 5 extra population while angry. Now it's 1.5 extra population per 1 unhappiness (from hurrying or drafting). And the 50% overall increase in foreign culture strength when angry is now adjusted to game speed (because the anger duration is longer in slower games) and taken times the square root of the unhappiness.
    
    Reduced the impact of religion in cases when neither the city owner nor the cultural owner have a state religion or when neither of those religions is present in the city.
    
    Instead of player tech era or game era, revolt chance now scales with a value computed from the percentage of techs discovered by cultural owner and city owner. That value gets quantized in order to avoid frequent changes in revolt probability.
    
    Related discussion on CFC:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-31#post-15735516

commit 67496f6b3173ad5ab1938952124eedf450f841d1
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Apr 13 21:00:10 2020 +0200

    Remove CvGlobals::m_aInfoVectors
    
    That was a vector containing (pointers to) all vectors of Cv...Info records. Filling that vector of vectors had involved an unsafe cast and BtS had only needed it for a function CvGlobals::infosReset that the EXE might never even call. In case that the EXE does call it, I've rewritten infosReset using the DO_FOR_EACH_INFO_TYPE macro originally added by change [advc.enum]. I.e. the vectors are now enumerated at compile time instead of being tracked at runtime.

commit 6d3e7b0f01343f7aa303c8540a88f297ac81ceb9
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Mon Apr 6 17:10:54 2020 +0200

    Tweak impact of city population on revolt chance
    
    Apply the era-based cap on the population factor _after_ shifting it toward the highest-ever population. And shift the population factor back toward the actual population eventually so that cities that stay small in the long run don't indefinitely get a revolt chance based on the highest-ever population.
    
    Prompted by this post by CFC user Lanstro:
    https://forums.civfanatics.com/threads/advanced-civ.614217/page-29#post-15723888

commit b6934e888877c3925a1ccf84de6c27a9d49d9623
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Apr 5 23:33:23 2020 +0200

    City trade tweaks
    
    [change id advc.ctr]
    
    Show a note in the city-conquered popup when the current target player for liberation differs from the target at peacetime (i.e. when liberation to the original owner is only possible through the city-conquered popup.
    
    AI again (as in BtS) says that "no such deal is possible" when asked what it will give in exchange for liberating a city.
    
    AI more reluctant to liberate a city for free when the recipient is the worst enemy of other relevant AI civs.
    
    Increased trade memory for liberation:
    * More lenient thresholds to determine that a liberated city is a major city or insignificant.
    * A single city of medium importance results in "+2: You liberated our cities" despite rounding.
    * Both sides' trade values are counted for fair trade and enemy trade memory, but still reduced a bit (because there's also liberation memory).
    * Fair/ enemy trade memory is also counted when ceding a city through the city-conquered popup.

commit 303786668f9ebfe4ffa29e7806504b258a86234e
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>

commit 507332fd0f239677826a773c0d543a5e9d23b92d
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Mar 29 16:47:05 2020 +0200

    Peace treaty in tribute/help deals; no treaty for vassals.
    
    When the AI asks for or demands an annual item (gold per turn, resource), a peace treaty gets included in the annual deal. So that all obligations expire together and automatically. (Automatic cancellation of peace treaties at the start of a game turn was already implemented.) Also more transparent: the peace treaty will now appear on the trade table. [advc.104m]
    
    And peace treaties now have a canTradeItem check that prevents vassals from signing one, i.e., after ending a war, only the master gets a peace treaty. (Vassals had already been unwilling to grant rival gift and tribute requests, so this additional change should only be relevant for peace treaties signed at the end of a war.) CvPlayer::forcePeace ignores the canTradeItem check, but I've replaced most forcePeace calls with CvTeam::signPeaceTreaty. forcePeace is used for giving vassals a peace treaty after a peacekeeping vote. [advc.130v]
    
    Revised [advc.032] (peace treaty signed during a peace treaty resets the old peace treaty) and [advc.130p] (trade value of peace not counted for diplo memory) to be compatible with the new changes.

commit fd5d755af022962c4e3e09495e052fbc80bf2457
Author: f1rpo <no.m@il.specified>
Date:   Sun Mar 22 17:52:47 2020 +0100

    AI code for city trade evaluation
    
    [change id advc.ctr]
    
    Some UWAI code revised and moved into a function AI_assetVal that is now used for both war evaluation and evaluation of city trades. AI_cityTradeVal rewritten, now also taking into account strategic factors like diplo attitude, victory stage and power ratio.
    
    Special treatment for liberated cities -- normally, I want to count no trade value for those (liberation player feels entitled to get it for free), but in some situations I want to count a reduced trade value and in some situations the full trade value.
    
    AI liberation memory based on the city's trade value.
    
    Non-liberation city trades result in a peace treaty.
    
    Tweaks to AI code for proposing city trades. Can now put more than one city on the table and regardless of at-war status. But AI code for initiating city trades is still to be done. Also to be done: More testing, profiling, documentation in manual (partly done), loading screen hints.
